<div class="object-language"><em>bá-bà-f-bá-bà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">bá-bà-f-bá-bà</div>
<div class="gloss">build-build-build-build</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he built many things' (not 'rebuilt the same things many times')</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (72)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>snà-n-sn-íyù tá x-á-n-áy-tán tá hlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">snà-n-sn-íyù</div>
<div class="gloss">hear-3-hear-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">x-á-n-áy-tán</div>
<div class="gloss">cut-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL-PO-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlà</div>
<div class="gloss">cow</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I heard them slaughter cows' (note that the object is not marked for plurality)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Cf.:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (73)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>snà-n-sn-íyù tá xn-áy-tán tá hlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">snà-n-sn-íyù</div>
<div class="gloss">hear-3-hear-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xn-áy-tán</div>
<div class="gloss">cut-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PO-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlà</div>
<div class="gloss">cow</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I heard them slaughter a cow'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

For bisyllabic verbs, the plural is formed by leftward repetition of the first syllable. In the perfective aspect the reduplicated theme of the verb is repeated twice:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (74)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɗá-ɗáxá-ná-f-ɗá-ɗáxá tá lgùt-á zwán-ì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗá-ɗáxá-ná-f-ɗá-ɗáxá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span>-sew-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP-PL</span>-sew</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lgùt-á</div>
<div class="gloss">dress-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zwán-ì</div>
<div class="gloss">child-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he sewed the children's clothing'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="Coding relationships between the predicate and noun phrases">Coding relationships between the predicate and noun phrases</h3>

The coding means for the relationship between the predicate and noun phrases include: the position directly after the verb; inherent properties of the verb; preposition _tá_; other prepositions; and verbal extensions. Several of these means may co-occur within the same clause.

The noun phrase (but not the prepositional phrase) directly following the verb in clauses other than sequential clauses is interpreted as subject:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (75)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dzà’á skwá-p-skwá nàsàrá-ngrá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzà’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FUT</span>-sew-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP-PL</span>-sew</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">skwá-p-skwá</div>
<div class="gloss">buy-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OUT</span>-buy</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nàsàrá-ngrá</div>
<div class="gloss">boss-black</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the black boss is going to sell . . .'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

In sequential clauses, there is no formal distinction between the nominal subject and the nominal object. In sentences containing sequential clauses, one usually expects the first clause to mention the subject, while subsequent clauses will not overtly mention the subject.. In the following example, the first clause has the subject following the verb. In the sequential clauses within the same sentence, the noun phrase that follows the verb is interpreted as object:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (76)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà hlí’yá-f-tá zvàxw kà ɗáwá-f-tá ntfàn ɗáwá-f-xà-tá dàwrà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span>-sew-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP-PL</span>-sew</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlí’yá-f-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">leave-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zvàxw</div>
<div class="gloss">bat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span>-sew-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP-PL</span>-sew</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗáwá-f-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">ask-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ntfàn</div>
<div class="gloss">glue</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗáwá-f-xà-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">ask-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-ALSO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dàwrà</div>
<div class="gloss">cloth</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the bat left and asked for glue and also for clothing'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="Preposition &lt;em&gt;tá&lt;/em&gt;">Preposition <em>tá</em></h3>

This section presents analyses different from the ones in Frajzyngier with Shay 2002 and includes some argumentation to support the new analyses. The form _tá_, qua preposition, indicates that the noun phrase that follows it is not the subject. As demonstrated throughout examples in the dictionary, this noun is very frequently the object of the clause:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (77)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsghà-k-tsghà 	tá ceedì </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsghà-k-tsghà </div>
<div class="gloss">send-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">INN</span>-send</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ceedì</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he sent money in'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (78)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xúxúrà-f-xúxúrà tá ghrùm tá sú </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xúxúrà-f-xúxúrà</div>
<div class="gloss">drill-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-drill</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghrùm</div>
<div class="gloss">hole</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sú</div>
<div class="gloss">tree</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he made a hole in a tree'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (79)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>zà-ná-ghú-zá ɗwàk tá dzúmá </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zà-ná-ghú-zá</div>
<div class="gloss">eat-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-SO</span>-eat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗwàk</div>
<div class="gloss">termite</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzúmá</div>
<div class="gloss">hay</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the termites have eaten part of the hay'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Not every complement of the preposition _tá_, however, is the direct object. Consider the verb _hlíná_ ‘warm up’. The verb is intransitive, as the entity that gets warmed up is always the subject. This verb cannot be used transitively, and yet this verb can have a complement marked by the preposition _tá_. The preposition indicates the source of heat:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (80)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hlíná-f-hlíná tá fìtík </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlíná-f-hlíná</div>
<div class="gloss">warm-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-warm</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fìtík</div>
<div class="gloss">fire</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he warmed up with the sun'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (81)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hlíná-f-hlíná tá vúvú  </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlíná-f-hlíná</div>
<div class="gloss">warm-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-warm</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vúvú </div>
<div class="gloss">fire</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he warmed up with the fire'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

One cannot say ‘the Sun warmed him up’ where the Sun is the subject and the third-person argument is the object. Similarly with the verb _búkwá_ ‘cover’: When it occurs with the affectedness of the subject extension, the verb means that the subject is being covered:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (82)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>búkwá-vá-búkw-í tá lgùt</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">búkwá-vá-búkw-í</div>
<div class="gloss">cover-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AS</span>-cover-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lgùt</div>
<div class="gloss">cloth</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I covered myself with a cloth'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The role of the noun phrase marked by the preposition _tá_ must be deduced from the inherent properties of the verb and/or from the extensions added to the verb. Thus, if the verb has the associative extension _ndá_, this extension forces the interpretation of the noun marked by _tá_ as an entity about which one thinks or remembers. With the verb _dúkwá_ ‘realize, become aware’ the associative extension marks the existence of the object of awareness:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (83)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkwá mbítsá tá pìtsákw-á-ní </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkwá</div>
<div class="gloss">realize-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-ASSC</span>-realize</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbítsá</div>
<div class="gloss">Mbítsá</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">pìtsákw-á-ní</div>
<div class="gloss">hoe-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Mbitsa has found about his hoe'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (84)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkw-ì tá sá-ghá-nì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkw-ì</div>
<div class="gloss">realize-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-ASSC</span>-realize-1SG</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sá-ghá-nì</div>
<div class="gloss">come-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:GO-GEN-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I became unexpectedly aware of his arrival'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

When the particle _tá_ precedes a verb or a clause, it marks the verb or clause as a comment on the preceding constituent, which may be clausal or nominal. Here is an example where the form _tá_ marks the comment on the element in focus:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (85)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tíngìl	vàzák tá lá-ghà tántán</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tíngìl</div>
<div class="gloss">first</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vàzák</div>
<div class="gloss">rooster</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-ghà</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:PVG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tántán</div>
<div class="gloss">first</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'It is Rooster that arrived first'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

In the following sentence, three noun phrases following the verb are preceded by the marker _tá_. In the first phrase the marker precedes the object, in the second it precedes the attribute of the object, and in the third it precedes the relative clause, i.e. the comment on the head of the relative clause:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (86)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɓàràká-f-ɓàràkú-lú tá tsá xàlá tá mndú	tá mtútà yá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɓàràká-f-ɓàràkú-lú</div>
<div class="gloss">celebrate-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-celebrate-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">HUM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàlá</div>
<div class="gloss">advanced age</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mndú</div>
<div class="gloss">man</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mtútà</div>
<div class="gloss">dead</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'One celebrated [through a trotting dance] the advanced age of the deceased (lit. 'of the person who died')'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="Point of view of the subject and goal orientation">Point of view of the subject and goal orientation</h3>

Both the point of view of the subject/source and goal orientation, i.e. indication that the event has a goal, are marked by verbal extensions. 

The point of view of the subject/source is marked in the perfective aspect by the extension _u_, which assumes the tone of the verb:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (87)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>z-ú-zà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">abwilyep</div>
<div class="gloss">eat-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-eat</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">this man is a sorcerer</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Some intransitive verbs must occur with the marker _u_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (88)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà mt-ú-tá dá-nì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mt-ú-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">die-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dá-nì</div>
<div class="gloss">father-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and his father died'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

In the imperfective aspect, the point of view of the subject is marked by the suffix _kú_, glossed as ABS (for ‘absolutive’) in Frajzyngier with Shay 2002:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (89)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xàɗ-áŋni tà mtà-kú ndá	mtà wà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàɗ-áŋni</div>
<div class="gloss">lack-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1PL:EXCL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mtà-kú</div>
<div class="gloss">die-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ABS</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mtà</div>
<div class="gloss">death</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'we do not die [when we are old]'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

When the noun that follows the verb is not preceded by a preposition, it is interpreted as the subject: 

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (90)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dr-ú-drá xàsúù</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dr-ú-drá</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàsúù</div>
<div class="gloss">wood</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the wood burned'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Coding the point of view of the subject is not a means of intransitivizing the verb. A verb coding the point of view of the subject can co-occur with an object marked by the preposition _tá_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (91)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hlr-ú-hlrà tá pìtsákw</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlr-ú-hlrà</div>
<div class="gloss">forge-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-forge</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">pìtsákw</div>
<div class="gloss">hoe</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he forged himself a hoe'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (92)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>nd-ù-ndà tá ghwánì </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nd-ù-ndà</div>
<div class="gloss">swallow-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-swallow</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghwánì</div>
<div class="gloss">medicine</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he swallowed the medicine'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (93)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>b-ù-bá tá xgà yà </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">b-ù-bá</div>
<div class="gloss">build-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-build</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xgà</div>
<div class="gloss">house</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he built himself a house'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The goal-orientation suffix _-a_ can be added either directly to the verbal root or to the point of view of subject marker _u_. In the sequence /C\[labial or velar\] u a/, the vowel _u_ is reduced to the feature \[round\], realized as labialization of the preceding consonant. The goal-oriented marker codes the event as directed toward a goal and thereby implies that the subject is controlling:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (94)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>fw-á-fwà tá ìmí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fw-á-fwà</div>
<div class="gloss">heat-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PVG</span>-heat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ìmí</div>
<div class="gloss">water</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he heated water'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Cf.:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (95)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>fú-fwà ìmí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fú-fwà</div>
<div class="gloss">heat up-heat up</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ìmí</div>
<div class="gloss">water</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'water heated up'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Consider the verb _ɗvà_ ‘like’. If the vowel _u_ is added to the stem ending in _á_, the meaning of the verb involves control on the part of the subject, resulting in meanings corresponding to ‘choose’, ‘select’, ‘prefer’:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (96)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà ɗvá-úgh-tá mákwà tá zvàxw</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗvá-úgh-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">like-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mákwà</div>
<div class="gloss">girl</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zvàxw</div>
<div class="gloss">bat</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the girl chose the bat [for herself]'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

If the vowel _u_ is added directly to the verbal root, the verbal stem means ‘to love’, a process that does not involve control:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (97)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà ɗv-ú-tá mákwà tá zvàxw</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗv-ú-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">like-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mákwà</div>
<div class="gloss">girl</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zvàxw</div>
<div class="gloss">bat</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the girl liked the bat'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="Classes of verbs">Classes of verbs</h3>

There are four classes of verbs, based on the inclusion or exclusion of a second nominal argument (‘transitivity’): unspecified; inherently transitive; inherently intransitive; and labile, i.e. both transitive and intransitive. 

<h4 id="Unspecified class">Unspecified class</h4>

An unspecified verb is a verb that does not inherently imply the presence or absence of an object. As a result, the presence of the third-person object must be overtly marked, and the absence of the object must also be overtly marked. With these verbs, the affectedness of the subject must also be overtly marked. The affectedness of the subject is marked by the point of view of subject extension -u or the affectedness of the subject extension _va_. Consider the verb _ɗífà_ ‘hide’. To indicate that the subject is the participant that hides himself, the point of view of subject marker _u_ must be used:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (98)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɗífà-u-ɗífà vàzák</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗífà-u-ɗífà</div>
<div class="gloss">hide-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-hide</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vàzák</div>
<div class="gloss">rooster</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the rooster hid himself'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

To indicate that the event has two participants, one controlling and the other undergoing the event, the verb must have the additional-argument marker _ná_ (glossed as DEM). The evidence that the marker _ná_ is not a third-person singular object pronoun is provided by the fact that it can co-occur with the verb in the plural form, implying the presence of multiple objects:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (99)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɗíf-ɗífà-ná-tà </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗíf-ɗífà-ná-tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span>-hide-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-REF</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'hide many things'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The nominal argument that follows the verb is interpreted as the subject of the transitive predication: 

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (100)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɗífà-ná-tà vàzák </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗífà-ná-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">hide-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vàzák</div>
<div class="gloss">rooster</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'it is the Rooster that hid him'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Consider now the verb _ghúyá_ ‘get drunk’. To indicate that the subject got drunk, the verb must have the point of view of the subject extension _u_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (101)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ghúy-ú-ghúyá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghúy-ú-ghúyá </div>
<div class="gloss">drink-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-drink</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he got drunk'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

To indicate that there is a participant who drank as a result of the action of somebody else, the marker _ná_ must be suffixed to the verb:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (102)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ghúy-ná-f-ghúy-ì </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghúy-ná-f-ghúy-ì </div>
<div class="gloss">drink-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP</span>-drink-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I made him drink'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Here is an example of the use of the extension _iŋ_, which allows the deployment of the second argument. The verb is _gúná_ ‘open’:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (103)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gún-iŋ-gúná tá sígà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gún-iŋ-gúná</div>
<div class="gloss">open-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AWAY</span>-open</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sígà</div>
<div class="gloss">pot</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he opened the pot'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (104)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gún-ú-gúná sígà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gún-ú-gúná</div>
<div class="gloss">open-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-open</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sígà</div>
<div class="gloss">pot</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the pot opened'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (105)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsá sígà tá gún-ú-tà yá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sígà</div>
<div class="gloss">pot</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gún-ú-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">open-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the pot that opened'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

And here is an example with the verb _làɓ_ ‘mix’:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (106)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>làɓ-ú-làɓá ɓìdá ndá vàrà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">làɓ-ú-làɓá</div>
<div class="gloss">mix-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-mix</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɓìdá</div>
<div class="gloss">millet</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vàrà</div>
<div class="gloss">beans</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'millet and beans got mixed up'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Compare with the additional-argument marker _ná_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (107)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>làɓà-ná-f-làɓá zwáŋà-ɗà tá ɓìdá ndá vàrà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">làɓà-ná-f-làɓá</div>
<div class="gloss">mix-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span>-mix</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zwáŋà-ɗà</div>
<div class="gloss">child:<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN-1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɓìdá</div>
<div class="gloss">millet</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vàrà</div>
<div class="gloss">bean</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'my child mixed up millet with beans'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (108)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ngá làɓà-ná-f-tà ndá ghúvà gù </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ngá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NORM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">làɓà-ná-f-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">mix-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP</span>-mix<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghúvà</div>
<div class="gloss">excrement</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gù</div>
<div class="gloss">goat</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'one should mix it with goat excrement'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Consider now the verb _dvà_ ‘threaten’. Without any morphological marking, the verb does not imply the presence of the second argument:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (109)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dvà-dvà </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dvà-dvà</div>
<div class="gloss">threaten-threaten</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he reprimanded, threatened' (no specific object or addressee is implied or can be inferred)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The addition of the second nominal argument requires the insertion of the additional argument marker _ná_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (110)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dvà-ná-ghá-dvá mbítsá tá zwànì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dvà-ná-ghá-dvá</div>
<div class="gloss">threaten-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-D:GO</span>-threaten</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbítsá</div>
<div class="gloss">Mbítsá</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zwànì</div>
<div class="gloss">children</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Mbitsa threatened children' (ná cannot be omitted)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h4 id="Inherently transitive verbs">Inherently transitive verbs</h4>

An inherently transitive verb takes a second argument, marked by the comment marker _tá_, without any changes to the verb. The third-person object is not overtly marked on the verb. Consider the verb _drà_ ‘burn’:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (111)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>drá-drà tá xàsú’ú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">drá-drà</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàsú’ú</div>
<div class="gloss">wood</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he burned wood [in order to get charcoal]'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

To code the point of view of the subject, and to indicate that the single noun phrase has undergone the event, the verb has the subject-oriented extension _u_ and the noun phrase follows the verb without a preposition:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (112)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dr-ú-drá xàsú’ù</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dr-ú-drá</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàsú’ú</div>
<div class="gloss">wood</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the wood burned'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The fact that the subject is undergoing the action can also be marked by the affectedness of the subject extension. The verb _gìgìɗà_ ‘shake a tree’ is inherently transitive, as evidenced by its use with the object marked by the preposition _tá_ (with tentative extension _n_):

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (113)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gìgìɗà-n-gìgìɗá tá fú </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gìgìɗà-n-gìgìɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">shake-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">TENT</span>-shake</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fú</div>
<div class="gloss">tree</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he shook the tree'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (114)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gìgìɗà-vá-gìgìɗá fú </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gìgìɗà-vá-gìgìɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">shake-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AS</span>-shake</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fú</div>
<div class="gloss">tree</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the tree shook'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

or:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (115)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gìgìɗ-ú-gìgìɗá fú </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gìgìɗ-ú-gìgìɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">shake-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-shake</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fú</div>
<div class="gloss">tree</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the tree shook'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The additional-argument marker _ná_ with an inherently transitive verb usually codes the presence of an indirect object in the proposition:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (116)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>drá-ná-drà (ngá-ní)</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">drá-ná-drà</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span>-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">(ngá-ní)</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FOR-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he burned it (for him)'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (117)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dr-íŋ-drá tá xàsú’ú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dr-íŋ-drá</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AWAY</span>-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàsú’ú</div>
<div class="gloss">wood</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he burned wood'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

To code coreferentiality of the subject and object, the verb must have the affectedness of the subject extension v and the object must be marked by the preposition _tá_, whose complement is the noun _vghá_ ‘body’ followed by a possessive pronoun:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (118)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dr-ú-v-drà tá vghá-ní</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dr-ú-v-drà</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-AS</span>-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vghá-ní</div>
<div class="gloss">vghá-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he burned himself'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Here is an example with the verb _bà_ ‘build’. The nominal object is marked by the comment marker _tá_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (119)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>b-í-dí-ɗí-f-bà tá xgá </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">b-í-dí-ɗí-f-bà</div>
<div class="gloss">build-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG-UP</span>-build</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xgá</div>
<div class="gloss">house</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he built me a house'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The addition of the marker _ná_ with an inherently transitive verb indicates the presence of an indirect object:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (120)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>bà-ná-f-bà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">bà-ná-f-bà </div>
<div class="gloss">build-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP</span>-build</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'build for someone'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h4 id="Inherently intransitive verbs">Inherently intransitive verbs</h4>

An intransitive verb is a verb that requires the additional-argument marker _ná_ to indicate that there are two arguments in the proposition. Without such a marker, the noun phrase that follows the verb is interpreted as the subject. This is the case with the verb _hànà_ ‘lie down’, ‘sleep’, ‘pass the night’:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (121)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hànà-hànà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hànà-hànà</div>
<div class="gloss">sleep-sleep</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he lay down/slept'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (122)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hànà-ná-hànà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hànà-ná-hànà</div>
<div class="gloss">sleep-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span>-sleep</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he made somebody lie down'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The presence of the additional-argument marker in the verb does not necessarily indicate the presence of either a direct or indirect object. It may indicate a presence of what in some Indo-European languages would correspond to adjunct: 

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (123)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hànà-ná-ghá-hànà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hànà-ná-ghá-hànà </div>
<div class="gloss">sleep-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-D:GO</span>-sleep</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'to lie on top of something'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

An inherently intransitive verb does not require any markers when it occurs with only one argument. Consider the verb _gə̀má_ ‘meet’:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (124)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gə̀má-f-gə̀má-xə̀n</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gə̀má-f-gə̀má-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss">meet-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-meet-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'they met'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

One can add an object to inherently intransitive verbs if the verb has the additional-argument marker _ná_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (125)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gə̀mà-ná-f-gə̀m-í tá xə̀n</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gə̀mà-ná-f-gə̀m</div>
<div class="gloss">meet-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP</span>-meet-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I got them together'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h4 id="Cognate object">Cognate object</h4>

A number of verbs are followed by cognate objects, i.e. objects linked semantically and phonologically with a specific verb. Such objects are marked by the comment marker _tá_. Cognate objects are often derived from the same root as the verb:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (126)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɗg-áy-tán tá ɗgú yá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗg-áy-tán</div>
<div class="gloss">thresh-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PO-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗgú̀</div>
<div class="gloss">threshing(N)</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá̀</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'While they were threshing'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Some intransitive verbs may be followed by an object marked by the preposition _tá_. These are, however, cognate objects. The cognate object may be followed by another object also marked by the comment marker _tá_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (127)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mbàzá-ná-mbàz-í tá mbàzá tá mbítsá </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbàzá-ná-mbàz-í</div>
<div class="gloss">wash-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span>-wash-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbàzá̀</div>
<div class="gloss">washing(N)</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbítsá</div>
<div class="gloss">Mbitsa</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I washed Mbitsa'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

An example of such a verb is _tsúhà_ ‘cough’:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (128)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsúhà-tsúhà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsúhà-tsúhà</div>
<div class="gloss">cough-cough</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he coughed'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (129)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsúh-ín-tsúhà tá másáɓì/màgàsàr</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsúh-ín-tsúhà</div>
<div class="gloss">cough-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AWAY</span>-cough</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">másáɓì/màgàsàr̀</div>
<div class="gloss">flu/tuberculosis</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he coughed the flu/tuberculosis' (the only objects allowed with this verb)'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Hence, the presence of the cognate object does not make the verb transitive.

<h4 id="Labile verbs">Labile verbs</h4>

There is a class of verbs (‘labile’ verbs) that are both intransitive and transitive, as evidenced by the fact that the presence of the third-person object is not overtly marked on the verb and the affectedness of the subject is not marked by the source-oriented marker _u_. One such verb is _hà_ ‘close’. Here is an example of a clause with two arguments. The object is marked only by the preposition _tá_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (130)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hà-f-hà tá txà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hà-f-hà</div>
<div class="gloss">close-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-close</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">txà</div>
<div class="gloss">door</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he closed the door'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (131)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hà-f-hà mbítsá tá txà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hà-f-hà</div>
<div class="gloss">close-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-close</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbítsá</div>
<div class="gloss">Mbitsa</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">txà</div>
<div class="gloss">door</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Mbitsa closed the door'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Here is an example of the clause with one argument, the subject. The affectedness of the subject is not marked by the source-orientation marker _u_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (132)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hà-f-hà txà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hà-f-hà</div>
<div class="gloss">close-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-close</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">txà</div>
<div class="gloss">door</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the door closed'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="The function of the object pronouns">The function of the object pronouns</h3>

The following chart represents object pronouns:

  

<table class="table table-bordered">
<caption>Table 12: Object suffixes</caption>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Person</th>
<th>Singular</th>
<th>Dual</th>
<th>Plural</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>First</td>
<td>í; ɗ; í-xà</td>
<td>úú</td>
<td>mú (incl); ŋní (excl)</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Second</td>
<td>ghá</td>
<td></td>
<td>ghúní</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Third</td>
<td>Ø; ná</td>
<td></td>
<td>xə̀n</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>

  

First- and second-person object pronouns can code the direct or indirect object, regardless of the verbs to which they are added. The form _ná_ with an inherently transitive verb codes the third-person singular indirect object:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (133)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>fáɗá-ná-fáɗá tá vwàx </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fáɗá-ná-fáɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">clean-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span>-clean</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vwàx</div>
<div class="gloss">field</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'clean the field for him'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

With other verbs, the form _ná_ suffixed to the verb indicates the presence of an additional participant, which may be a direct object. The form ná is used even if the direct object is plural, which is the evidence that ná is not the third-person singular object marker:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (134)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dzrà-ná-f-dzrù-lù tá xǝ̀n </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzrà-ná-f-dzrù-lù</div>
<div class="gloss">agree-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG-UP</span>-agree-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">HUM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xǝ̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'one has made them agree'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Compare the intransitive:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (135)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dzrà-p-dzrá-xǝ̀n</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzrà-p-dzrá-xǝ̀n</div>
<div class="gloss">agree-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OUT</span>-agree-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'they agreed with each other'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The first-person singular object affixes are _i_, _i-xà_, and _ɗa_. The form _ɗa_ is a cognate of the first-person possessive marker ɗá. The pronoun i replaces the vowel of the preceding verb and assumes its grammatical tone, i.e. the tone that the verb has before the direct object:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (136)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ks-ì-ksà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ks-ì-ksà</div>
<div class="gloss">touch-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span>-touch</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he touched me' or 'he wounded me' (<em>ksá</em> 'catch him/it!' has underlying high tone)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (137)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kzl-ì-kzlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kzl-ì-kzlà</div>
<div class="gloss">wait-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span>-wait</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he waited for me' (<em>kzlà</em> has underlying low tone)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The form _ixà_ is equivalent to the form _i_. The form _ixa_ occurs optionally when there are no other extensions to the verb:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (138)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kzl-ìxà-kzlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kzl-ìxà-kzlà</div>
<div class="gloss">wait-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span>-wait</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he waited for me' (<em>kzlà</em> has underlying low tone)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (139)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ks-ìxà-ksà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ks-ìxà-ksà</div>
<div class="gloss">touch-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span>-touch</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he touched me' or 'he wounded me'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The form _ɗ_ is used if the verb has the stem-formative movement-away marker _í_, the point-of view of the subject marker _ú_, or some other extension(s):

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (140)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>hl-ì-ɗ-á-ghá-hlà	[hl-ì-ɗáa-hlà]</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hl-ì-ɗ-á-ghá-hlà</div>
<div class="gloss">fall-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AWAY-1SG-PVG-D:PVG</span>-fall</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he found me' (The verb <em>hlà</em> 'fall' is intransitive, and the marker <em>i</em> has a transitivizing function here.)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (141)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mántsá yá ká-xə̀n mb-ì-ɗí-f-tà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mántsá</div>
<div class="gloss">like that</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mb-ì-ɗí-f-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">cure-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AWAY-1SG-UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'that is how they cured me'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="Reciprocal">Reciprocal</h3>

The reciprocal function is coded by the plural subject pronoun on the verb and the noun _vghá_ ‘body’ preceded by the preposition _tá_. The difference between the reciprocal and the marking of coreferentiality is that in the reciprocal the noun _vghá_ ‘body’ is not followed by a possessive pronoun coding the person and number of the subject:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (142)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tskáy, tà tsk-áy-lú tá vghá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tskáy,</div>
<div class="gloss">gathering</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsk-áy-lú</div>
<div class="gloss">gather:<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">POT-HUM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vghá</div>
<div class="gloss">body</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'do people gather as they used to?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (143)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>gúyá-f-gúyà xə̀n tá vghá ndá zwánì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gúyá-f-gúyà</div>
<div class="gloss">meet-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-meet</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vghá</div>
<div class="gloss">body</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zwánì</div>
<div class="gloss">children</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'they met with children'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<h3 id="Indirect object">Indirect object</h3>

Hdi has the category ‘indirect object’ which represents an entity C, often animate, such that when A acts on B it affects C or when the event has only one participant A, but the non-participant in the event C is affected. The nature of the affectedness is not indicated, and it may be benefactive, malefactive, or have no value in the moral domain. The way the indirect object is marked depends on the type of verb and the person of the indirect object. With verbs that do not inherently imply the presence of an indirect object, the pronoun is marked for the indirect object function through high tone on the last syllable of the verb:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (144)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>pɗ-íxà-pɗá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">pɗ-íxà-pɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">leave-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span>-leave</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he left it for me'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Cf.:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (145)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>pɗ-ìxà-pɗà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">pɗ-ìxà-pɗà</div>
<div class="gloss">leave-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span>-leave</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I was abandoned/he left me'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (146)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kl-í-g-í-ɗá-ghà wá kɗìx-á-ɗá, ká-’á kà wàxú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kl-í-g-í-ɗá-ghà</div>
<div class="gloss">take-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">EP-INN-AWAY-1SG-D:PVG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kɗìx-á-ɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">donkey-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN-1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss">like</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wàxú</div>
<div class="gloss">cry</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'"Bring me back my donkey", he said, crying'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (147)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɓlá-ghà-p-ɓlá tá ùdzú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɓlá-ghà-p-ɓlá</div>
<div class="gloss">break-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG-OUT</span>-break</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ùdzú</div>
<div class="gloss">stick</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he broke your stick' (to your cetriment)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Direct affectedness is coded by low tone on the verb and high tone on the pronoun:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (148)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɓlà-ghá-p-ɓlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɓlà-ghá-p-ɓlà</div>
<div class="gloss">break-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG-OUT</span>-break</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he broke you'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

Verbs that inherently involve an indirect object, which in Hdi include _vlá_ ‘give’ and _mná_ ‘tell’, require the indirect object marker. The unspecified indirect object is marked by the suffix _n_, glossed as 3 (third person) in Frajzyngier with Shay 2002:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (149)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>vlá-n-vl-í tá kóɓù</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-n-vl-í</div>
<div class="gloss">give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3</span>-give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kóɓù</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I gave money'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

The marker _n_ also occurs with such verbs if the indirect object is an independent pronoun, e.g. the third-person plural pronoun _xə̀n_ or a noun. The independent pronoun and the nouns are marked by the preposition _tá_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (150)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>vlá-n-vl-íyù tá xə̀n tá kóɓù</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-n-vl-íyù</div>
<div class="gloss">give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3</span>-give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kóɓù</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I gave him money'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

or:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (151)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>vlá-n-vl-í tá kóɓù tá xə̀n</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-n-vl-í</div>
<div class="gloss">give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3</span>-give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kóɓù</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I gave them money'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (152)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>vlá-n-vlá mbítsá tá kóɓù tá mbáká</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-n-vlá</div>
<div class="gloss">give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3</span>-give</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbítsá</div>
<div class="gloss">Mbitsa</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kóɓù</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>

</div>
</div>
