</div>
</div>
</div>

If there is a specific indirect object in the proposition, the indirect object is coded by an object pronoun. For the third person, the marker is _ná_:

<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (153)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>vlá-ná-vl-í tá kóɓù</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-ná-vl-í</div>
<div class="gloss">give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span>-give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kóɓù</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I gave him (specific person) money'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>With all other verbs, the third-person indirect object is marked by the additional-argument marker <em>ná</em>. The benefactive function of the indirect object is marked by the preposition <em>ngá</em> preceding a noun or a pronoun:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (154)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>drá-ná-drà (ngá-ní)</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">drá-ná-drà</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span>-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">(ngá-ní)</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FOR-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I burned it (for him)'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<br clear="both"/>
<h3 id="Adjuncts">Adjuncts</h3>
<p>The term ‘adjuncts’ refers to semantic roles that can be added to any predicate. Moreover, adjuncts can be added to clauses that already have either a subject or object or both. The roles of all adjuncts are marked by prepositions. As we have seen with the preposition <em>tá</em>, not every prepositional phrase marks an adjunct.</p>
<p>The preposition <em>kà</em> marks a semantic role that represents the result of the transformation of one entity into another:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (155)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà d-ù-tà kà ghzú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">d-ù-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">cook-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AS/INTO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghzú</div>
<div class="gloss">beer</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and she transformed it into beer'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The associative preposition <em>ndà</em> ‘with, by’ marks a co-participant in the event, the instrumental argument, and time:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (156)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mbù’á-vá-mbù’á tá ɗáfà ndá hlìhlík </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbù’á-vá-mbù’á</div>
<div class="gloss">eat.without.the.sauce-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AS</span>-eat.without.the.sauce</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗáfà</div>
<div class="gloss">mush</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss">with</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlìhlík</div>
<div class="gloss">eggs</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he ate mush with eggs but without the sauce'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (157)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kàp-á-n-kàpá xdí tá ghǝ̀ŋ ndá hàmanyàjì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kàp-á-n-kàpá</div>
<div class="gloss">raise-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GO-TENT</span>-raise</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xdí</div>
<div class="gloss">Hdi</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghǝ̀ŋ</div>
<div class="gloss">head</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hàmanyàjì</div>
<div class="gloss">Hamman Yaji </div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Hdi tried to make an uprising against Hamman Yaji'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The prepositions <em>dá</em> and <em>dà</em> mark locative arguments of the verbs of movement. The preposition with the high tone, <em>dá</em>, is used when the complement is a place name or an inherently locative adverb:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (158)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>vàlà-dá-p-vàl-í dá xàdà á </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vàlà-dá-p-vàl-í</div>
<div class="gloss">jump-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ALL-OUT</span>-jump-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">TO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàdà</div>
<div class="gloss">here</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I jumped all the way there'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The form with the low tone, <em>dà</em>, is used when the following noun is not a place name or an inherent locative: </p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (158)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsìɗà-dá-m-tsìɗà mdú-xà dà dzùgùví </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsìɗà-dá-m-tsìɗà</div>
<div class="gloss">enter-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ALL-IN</span>-enter</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mdú-xà</div>
<div class="gloss">people-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">TO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzùgùví</div>
<div class="gloss">room</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'a crowd entered the room'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The preposition <em>tà</em> marks the locative stative complement:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (160)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ndá ǹgh-í tà ptà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">STAT</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ǹgh-í</div>
<div class="gloss">see-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ptà</div>
<div class="gloss">mat</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I saw it on the mat'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The preposition <em>mà</em> is a spatial specifier indicating the location of an object or event within the space of the locative complement:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (161)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">

</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tàbá</div>
<div class="gloss">center</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">

</div>

</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'among these children of Kderi'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The preposition <em>gà</em> ‘inner space’ locates the event or object within the deictic center or as directed toward or from inside the deictic center:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (162)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">

<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ìm</div>
<div class="gloss">water</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gà</div>
<div class="gloss">in</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xdí</div>
<div class="gloss">Hdi</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">

<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>

<div class="morpheme">kó</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q (H)</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'So, there are no rains in Hdi?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The benefactive adjunct is marked by the preposition <em>ngá</em> ‘for’:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">

</div>

</div>

</div>

<h2 id="Verbal Extensions">Verbal Extensions</h2>
<h3 id="Introduction">Introduction</h3>
<p>The term ‘verbal extensions’ designates suffixes to the verb that are not subject, object, or TAM markers. The full description of the functions of various extensions is to be found in Frajzyngier with Shay 2002. Verbal extensions are suffixed to the simple form of the verb or infixed between the reduplicated forms of the verb. Verbal extensions constitute the principal formal means to code the following: point of view; the affectedness of the subject function; the semantic relation of the subject; the semantic relation of the second argument marked by the preposition <em>tá</em>; the directionality of the event; the manner in which the event is performed; and the spatial relations with respect to the locative target. The extensions coding directionality and spatial orientation are segmentally similar to locative prepositions. There is a strict ordering of extensions: Extensions modifying the manner of event are followed by extensions coding the semantic roles of arguments, and these are followed by extensions coding the directionality of the event and spatial orientation with respect to the locative center.</p>
<h3 id="Manner extensions">Manner extensions</h3>
<p>Three extensions code the manner of the event: <em>gl</em>, the ‘do again’ extension; <em>n</em> or <em>ŋ</em>, the ‘tentative’ extension; and <em>ndá</em>, the ‘associative’ extension. The extension <em>gl</em> indicates repetition of the action after some time, as opposed to plurality of the action, which is coded by the infix <em>á</em> or by reduplication of the verb:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (165)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>sə̀-gl-s-í</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sə̀-gl-s-í</div>
<div class="gloss">drink-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AGAIN</span>-drink-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I drank again'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (166)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà másə́-gl-tá-tsí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">másə́-gl-tá-tsí</div>
<div class="gloss">apply.ointment-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AGAIN-REF-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and he was again applying the ointment'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The tentative extension indicates an attempt to perform an action or partial execution of an action:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (167)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ghùɓàsá-n-ghùɓàsá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghùɓàsá-n-ghùɓàsá</div>
<div class="gloss">laugh-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">TENT</span>-laugh</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he laughed a bit'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (168)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tà-n-tà tá sígà </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà-n-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">burst-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">TENT</span>-burst</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sígà</div>
<div class="gloss">pot</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he tried to burst the pot'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The affectedness of the subject extension v indicates that the event applies to the subject and that the subject is affected. It is different from the subject-oriented extension, as illustrated by the following examples with the transitive verb <em>nù’á</em> ‘fatten’:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (169)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>nù’ú-v-nù’à tá hlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nù’ú-v-nù’à</div>
<div class="gloss">fatten-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AS</span>-fatten</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlà</div>
<div class="gloss">cow</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he fattened a cow for himself'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (170)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>nù’-ú-nù’á hlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nù’-ú-nù’á</div>
<div class="gloss">fatten-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-fatten</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlà</div>
<div class="gloss">cow</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the cow is fattened'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Compare the same verb with the extension <em>f</em> ‘up’:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (171)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>nù’á-f-nù’á tá hlà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nù’á-f-nù’á</div>
<div class="gloss">fatten-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span>-fatten</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlà</div>
<div class="gloss">cow</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he fattened the cow(s)'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The associative extension <em>ndá</em> codes the presence of the associative participant in the proposition, whether the participant is present in the clause or not. When overtly present, such a participant is marked by the preposition <em>tá</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (172)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkwá mbítsá tá pìtsákw-á-ní </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkwá</div>
<div class="gloss">find-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-ASSC</span>-find</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbítsá</div>
<div class="gloss">Mbitsa</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">pìtsákw-á-ní</div>
<div class="gloss">hoe-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Mbitsa has found out about his hoe'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (173)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkw-ì tá sá-ghá-nì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dúkwá-f-ndá-dúkw-ì</div>
<div class="gloss">find-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-ASSC</span>-find-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sá-ghá-nì</div>
<div class="gloss">hoe-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I became unexpectedly aware of his arrival'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3 id="Locative extensions">Locative extensions</h3>
<p>Locative extensions consist of the following groups, arranged in the order they occupy after the verb and the way in which they can be combined. Members within a given group cannot be combined with one another. With the verb being the leftmost component, the extensions are organized as follows:</p>
<br/>
<table class="table table-bordered">
<caption>Table 13: Locative extensions</caption>
<thead>
<tr>
<th>Group 1</th>
<th>Group 2</th>
<th>Group 3</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>g ‘inner space’</td>
<td>gh ‘distal’</td>
<td>f ‘movement up’</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>dá ‘allative’</td>
<td></td>
<td>p ‘movement out’</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td></td>
<td></td>
<td>xà ‘movement down’</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td></td>
<td></td>
<td>m ‘movement in’</td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<br/>
<p>The goal-oriented marker <em>á</em> (GO) must follow the verb whenever one of the spatial extensions from the set comprising <em>f</em> ‘movement up’, <em>p</em> ‘movement out’, <em>xà</em> ‘movement down’, <em>dá</em> ‘allative’, <em>m</em> ‘movement in’ and <em>g</em> ‘inner space orientation’ is added. </p>
<p>The distal extension <em>gh</em>, which indicates an event outside of the place of speech, can be combined with the source-oriented marker u or with the goal marker <em>á</em>. Compare the following examples, all in the prohibitive mood. The first one has no extension, and the remaining have various locative extensions:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (174)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mà kə́l-ká</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PROH</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kə́l-ká</div>
<div class="gloss">take-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'do not take it'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (175)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mà kl-á-ghá-ká</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PROH</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kl-á-ghá-ká</div>
<div class="gloss">take-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GO-D:GO-2SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'do not take it there'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (176)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>drá-ghú-drá tá nìvì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">drá-ghú-drá</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:SO</span>-burn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nìvì</div>
<div class="gloss">firewood</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he burned firewood only'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Locative extensions can be combined with extensions from other domains as well:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (177)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>drà-ná-ghú-drà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">drà-ná-ghú-drà</div>
<div class="gloss">burn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">TENT-D:SO</span>-burn</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he burned a part [of the firewood]'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (178)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà ghùɓàsá-p-tá lá jíjì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghùɓàsá-p-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">laugh-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OUT-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá</div>
<div class="gloss">people</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">jíjì</div>
<div class="gloss">in-laws</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the in-laws burst out laughing mocking him'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>One of the most important properties of locative spatial extensions is that, in addition to coding the relationship to the locative target or source, they also code the associated event, most frequently the movement associated with the event represented by the verb to which the extensions have been added. Thus the distal extension <em>gh</em> codes movement of the subject and or object toward the locative target. The example below contains only two verbs, <em>lá</em> ‘go’ and <em>ksà</em> ‘catch’, the latter with three extensions. The extension <em>g</em> indicates spatial orientation (INN), and the extension <em>gh</em> indicates the associated movement. As a result, the translation has three rather than two propositions:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (179)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ngá lá-bà m̀ndú-xà ksà-gá-ghà-tà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ngá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NORM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-bà</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OUT</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">m̀ndú-xà</div>
<div class="gloss">man-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ksà-gá-ghà-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">catch-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">INN-D:PVG-REF:SUBJ</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'people should go out, catch him, and bring him back'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Compare also two propositions with one verb in the following example:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (180)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà là-gá-ghà-tá-tsí tá hlrə́ŋ-á fú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">là-gá-ghà-tá-tsí</div>
<div class="gloss">dig-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">INN-D:PVG-REF-3SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlrə́ŋ-á</div>
<div class="gloss">root-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fú</div>
<div class="gloss">tree</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'she dug and brought a root of a certain tree'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The following example illustrates the functions of some locative extensions with the verb <em>ɓlà</em> ‘break’:</p>
<ul>
<li><em>ɓl-íŋ-ɓlà</em> 			‘break and leave’</li>
<li><em>ɓlà-gá-ghà-ɓlà</em> 			‘break and bring here’</li>
<li><em>ɓlá-ná-ghá-ɓlá </em>			‘break and add’</li>
</ul>
<p>The associated-event characteristic of verbal extensions removes, to a large degree, the motivation for the existence of coordinating clausal conjunction equivalent to ‘and’, whose function would be to indicate that the two clauses are part of a single sentence.  </p>
<h2 id="Modality">Modality</h2>
<p>The speaker’s assertion is the unmarked modality in Hdi. Hypothetical modality may be coded by the clause-initial particle <em>bá</em> and clause-final particle <em>ɓà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (181)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ká ùvá mántsá bá tà dzà-í ɓá </em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ùvá</div>
<div class="gloss">cat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mántsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">bá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">HYP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzà-í</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɓá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">HYP</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Cat said:" I might go but . . ."'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hypothetical modality may also be marked by the form <em>má</em> followed by the referential past tense marker <em>sí</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (182)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ká ùvá mántsá má sí tà dzá-í mndán . . .</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ùvá</div>
<div class="gloss">cat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mántsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">má</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">HYP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sí</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PAST</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzà-í</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mndán</div>
<div class="gloss">but</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Cat answered:" I might go but . . ."'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There is a class of epistemic adverbs all occurring in clause-initial position, e.g.:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (183)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>pàtə̀k ndá mà ghwà tá bgàhlà,</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">pàtə̀k</div>
<div class="gloss">perhaps</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IN</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghwà</div>
<div class="gloss">river</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">bgàhlà</div>
<div class="gloss">Bgahla</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'perhaps in the direction of the river Bgahla'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The imperative verb stem is identical with the indicative stem. The language makes a morphological distinction between singular (unmarked) and plural addressees, marked by the suffix <em>wá</em> in the imperative:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (184)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kl-í-g-í-ɗá-ghà-wá kɗìx-á-ɗà, ká-’á</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kl-í-g-í-ɗá-ghà-wá</div>
<div class="gloss">take-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">EP-INN-AWAY-1SG-GO-PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kɗìx-á-ɗà</div>
<div class="gloss">donkey-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN-1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'"Bring me the donkey", he said'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The reduplicated form of the verb is used in the imperative to code bounded events. In the imperative mood with a non-reduplicated verb, the second argument is coded only by the position following the verb, rather than by the preposition <em>tá</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (185)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mbsá-f sígà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbsá-f</div>
<div class="gloss">cover-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sígà</div>
<div class="gloss">pot</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'cover the pot!'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There is a distinct subjunctive mood in Hdi, marked by the sequential marker <em>kà</em> and the verb ending in the vowel <em>a</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (186)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà zá Pghìntà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zá</div>
<div class="gloss">eat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">Pghìntà</div>
<div class="gloss">Phinta</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'Phinta should eat'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The subjunctive mood contrasts with the indicative mood, where the verb is represented only by the consonant(s), plus epenthetic vowel as required by syllable structure conditions. The subject is overtly coded in the subjunctive mood:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (187)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà zə́	Pghìntà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zə</div>
<div class="gloss">eat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">Pghìntà</div>
<div class="gloss">Phinta</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and Phinta ate'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The second argument is preceded by the preposition <em>tá</em> in the subjunctive mood, just as in the indicative mood:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (188)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà wùdá-xə̀n tá wùdá	ká-’á</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wùdá-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss">fight-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wùdá</div>
<div class="gloss">fight</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he said that they should fight'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (189)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà wùdə́-xə̀n	tá wùdá	ká-’á</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wùdə́-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss">fight-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wùdá</div>
<div class="gloss">fight</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and he said that they fight'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There are distinct forms to code the subjunctive in perfective aspect ( cf. Frajzyngier with Shay 2002, Chapter 11, section 6).</p>
<p>Hdi has the prohibitive mood, marked by the particle <em>mà</em> preceding the verb, to which subject pronouns are suffixed:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (190)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mà tágh-ká tá skál-á m̀ndú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PROH</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tágh-ká</div>
<div class="gloss">learn-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">skál-á</div>
<div class="gloss">dance-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">m̀ndú</div>
<div class="gloss">man</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'do not learn the dance of others' (i.e. go your own way)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Aspect">Aspect</h2>
<p>The language makes a distinction between the perfective, imperfective, and stative aspect. With respect to the perfective and imperfective aspect, there are two systems. One occurs in affirmative indicative clauses, in yes/no questions, and in comments on topicalized constituents. These types of clauses do not require any specific presupposition for their proper semantic interpretation and are therefore pragmatically independent clauses.</p>
<p>The other aspectual system occurs in comment-on-focus constructions, relative clauses, content questions, and presentative constructions. All of these clauses are comments on a proposition that has been previously mentioned in discourse or require a specific discourse presupposition for their interpretation. These are pragmatically dependent clauses (Frajzyngier 2004). Table 14 shows the means of coding aspect in the two types of clauses:</p>
<br/>
<table class="table table-bordered">
<caption>Table 14: Aspectual system</caption>
<thead>
<tr>
<th></th>
<th>Independent</th>
<th>Dependent</th>
</tr>
</thead>
<tbody>
<tr>
<td>Perfective</td>
<td>reduplication</td>
<td>verb-a</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Imperfective</td>
<td>tà nominalized verb</td>
<td>tà verbal root</td>
</tr>
<tr>
<td>Stative</td>
<td>ndá verb-a</td>
<td></td>
</tr>
</tbody>
</table>
<br/>
<p>Hdi also has the progressive aspect, marked by the form <em>tà</em> followed by the reduplicated form of the verb with the potential suffix <em>-a</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (191)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tà z-áy-z-áy tá ɗàfá kùl xàɗ(ú) ɗàlí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">z-áy-z-áy</div>
<div class="gloss">eat-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PO</span>-eat-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗàfá</div>
<div class="gloss">mush</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kùl</div>
<div class="gloss">without</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàɗ(ú)</div>
<div class="gloss">lack</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗàlí</div>
<div class="gloss">sauce</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he is eating mush without the sauce'	(action going on right now)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Tense">Tense</h2>
<p>There are only two tense categories: the referential past and the future. The referential past is marked by the particle <em>sí</em> at the beginning of the clause. The form designates events that happened at some well-determined point in time that is included in the clause or that can be recovered from the previous discourse:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (192)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ká-xə̀n mántsá, sí ndá	gá ká ndá rvíɗìk</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mántsá</div>
<div class="gloss">like.that</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sí</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PAST</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gá</div>
<div class="gloss">where</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">rvíɗìk</div>
<div class="gloss">night</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and they said:"Where were you last night?"'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Three constructions code future tense. In one, the verb <em>dzà’á</em> ‘go’ is used with the perfective aspect:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (193)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dzà’á	phlá-phlá-xə̀ŋ tá m̀ndú</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzà’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FUT</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">phlá-phlá-xə̀ŋ</div>
<div class="gloss">kill.<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span>-kill.<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">m̀ndú</div>
<div class="gloss">man</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'they will kill [all of us] . . .'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In another future tense construction, the form <em>dzà’á</em> ‘go’ is used with the imperfective aspect:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (194)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dzà’á hlə̀v-áy tá índà m̀ndú-xà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzà’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FUT</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlə̀v-áy</div>
<div class="gloss">hit-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">índà</div>
<div class="gloss">all</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">m̀ndú</div>
<div class="gloss">man-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he will hit everybody'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In the third future tense construction, the simple verb stem is used without the auxiliary verb. This construction is deployed in negative clauses:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (195)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ks-ú-tà á krì tá ùvá wà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ks-ú-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">devour-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">krì</div>
<div class="gloss">dog</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ùvá</div>
<div class="gloss">cat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the dog will not devour the cat'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Compare the affirmative future:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (196)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà dzà’á krì ks-ú-tá ùvá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzà’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FUT</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">krì</div>
<div class="gloss">dog</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ks-ú-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">devour-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ùvá</div>
<div class="gloss">cat</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and the dog will devour the cat'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Question Formation">Question Formation</h2>
<h3 id="Polar questions">Polar questions</h3>
<p>The interrogative mood is coded by (further) raising the last tone of the clause:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (197)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>vlá-ghá-vlá-xə̀n tá kób-à-ɗá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-ghá-vlá-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss">give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span>-give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kób-à-ɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">money-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN-1SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'did they give you my money?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another means of forming polar questions is through the clause-final particles <em>rà</em>, <em>rí</em>, <em>rè</em>, or <em>r-kè</em>. The markers <em>rí</em> and <em>rà</em> are interchangeable and do not imply the speaker’s assumptions about the truth of the proposition:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (198)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xànà-xàná-ká rà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-ghá-vlá-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss">spend.night-spend.night-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">rà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'did you spend the night well?' (greeting in the morning)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>A rhetorical question about the truth may be marked by the interjection <em>kí</em> or <em>ké</em> added to the general interrogative marker <em>rà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (199)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xd-íyù r-ké</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xd-íyù</div>
<div class="gloss">Hdi-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">r-ké</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q-INTERJ</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'am I Hdi?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cf.:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (200)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xd-íyù rà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xd-íyù</div>
<div class="gloss">Hdi-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">rà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'am I Hdi?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h3 id="Content questions">Content questions</h3>
<p>Content questions differ from polar questions in the aspectual system used, the question words used, 
    and the clause-final interrogative marker, which is <em>nà</em> rather than <em>rà</em>.
    The clause-final question marker <em>nà</em> is not obligatory. 
    Content questions are characterized by use of the dependent perfective and imperfective aspects. 
    The following semantic categories are coded in content questions: human participant, coded by the question word <em>wá</em>;
    non-human participant, coded by the question words <em>nə́</em> in the de dicto domain and <em>nú</em> in the de re domain; 
    questions about place, coded by the question word <em>gá</em>; questions about time coded by the question word, <em>yà</em>; 
    questions about manner, coded by the question word <em>kí</em>; and reason, marked by the form <em>nə́</em> ‘what’ followed by the 
    copula <em>yà</em>, realized as <em>ní-yà</em>. The language also codes the grammatical role of the argument that the question is about, specifically the categories subject, object, indirect object, 
    and associative, and questions about the heads of the modifying construction. Content questions about a non-human participant also code, through different forms of the question word, 
    whether the event is referential or not. </p>
<p>In questions about the subject of equational clause, the subject precedes the predicate and the interrogative modality is marked by the clause-final particle <em>nà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (201)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>wá ɗghá nà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wá</div>
<div class="gloss">who</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗghá</div>
<div class="gloss">blacksmith</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'who is a blacksmith?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The role of the interrogative word as subject or object of the clause is computed from the absence or presence of other subjects and objects in the clause. Thus if the verb contains information about the subject, e.g. a subject pronoun, the clause-initial question word is interpreted as the object. This is illustrated on question words about an inanimate object from the domain de dicto, marked by the form <em>nə́</em>, and from the domain de re, marked by the form <em>nú</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (202)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>nə́ bà-f-tsí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nə</div>
<div class="gloss">what</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">bà-f-tsí</div>
<div class="gloss">build<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'what did he build?' (The set of potential objects is wide open.)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (203)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>nú bà-f-tsí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nú</div>
<div class="gloss">which thing</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">bà-f-tsí</div>
<div class="gloss">build<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'which one did he build?' (The set of potential objects is known to the speaker.)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>If the verb does not contain the subject marker, the clause-initial question word is interpreted as the subject:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (204)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>nə́ tá klà-gá-ghá-f-tà tà ná fú ná nà	ká-’á</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nə</div>
<div class="gloss">what</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">klà-gá-ghá-f-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">take<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">INN-2SG-UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">fú</div>
<div class="gloss">tree</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'"What brought you here to this tree?", he asked'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>There is a special form for questions about human plural subjects, marked by the question word <em>wá</em> preceded by the associative pluralmarker <em>ì</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (205)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ì wá tá phlà-ná-p-tà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ì</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC.PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wá</div>
<div class="gloss">who</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">phlà-ná-p-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">break-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'who were the people who broke it?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Questions about the indirect object have the marker <em>ná</em> in the verb, followed by the form <em>wá</em> if the indirect object is human:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (206)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dà-ná-tá wá-ká tá ɗàfá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dà-ná-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">cook-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wá-ká</div>
<div class="gloss">who-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗàfá</div>
<div class="gloss">food</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'for whom did you cook?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The form <em>wá</em> also serves as a question word for questions about manner. The interpretation that the manner is in the scope of the question word is ensured by the presence of the overt marker of the subject in the clause:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (207)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>wá ká Mbitsa lá-ghú-í dá Nigeria</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wá</div>
<div class="gloss">how</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">Mbitsa</div>
<div class="gloss">Mbitsa</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-ghú-í</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:SO-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">Nigeria</div>
<div class="gloss">Nigeria</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'how did Mbitsa go to Nigeria from here?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The question about reason is marked by the clause-initial particle <em>ngú</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (208)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ngú tà zá ká</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ngú</div>
<div class="gloss">why</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zá</div>
<div class="gloss">eat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'why do you eat?' (if you were told not to eat)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Negation of pragmatically independent clauses">Negation of pragmatically independent clauses</h2>
<p>Negation of pragmatically independent clauses has the form <em>a . . . wà</em>, with the marker <em>a</em> following the predicate and preceding the subject, and the marker <em>wà</em> following the object and adjuncts, if any. The final vowel <em>à</em> on the negative marker may be deleted in clause-medial position and replaced by an epenthetic vowel for the syllabification purposes:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (209)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ɗvà ‘á xdí-xà tá l’école wù, ká-’á</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗvà</div>
<div class="gloss">like</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">‘á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xdí-xà</div>
<div class="gloss">Hdi-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">l’école</div>
<div class="gloss">school (fr.)</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wù</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'"Hdi do not like school", he said'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (210)
</div>
<div class="sentence"> <div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xámáyádzì á wà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xámáyádzì</div>
<div class="gloss">Hamayadzi</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'it is not Haman Yaji'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Negation in the pragmatically dependent clause is marked by the form <em>xàɗú</em> at the beginning of the clause and the clause-final marker <em>wà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (211)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xàɗ áŋni tà mtà-kú ndá	mtà wà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàɗ</div>
<div class="gloss">lack</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">áŋni</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1PL:EXCL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mtà-kú</div>
<div class="gloss">die-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ABS</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mtà</div>
<div class="gloss">die</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'we do not die [when we are old]'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Negation of possessive clauses has the form of negation of locative clauses, with the form <em>xàɗú</em> at the beginning of the clause and the clause-final marker <em>wà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (212)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xàɗ kóɓ dà tsí wà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàɗ</div>
<div class="gloss">lack</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kóɓ</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsí</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'he/she does not have any money'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Topicalization">Topicalization</h2>
<p>There are different means of topicalization for different grammatical roles and different lexical categories.</p>
<p>The pronominal subject in the imperfective clause is topicalized through the use of an independent pronoun rather than a subject pronoun after the verb:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (213)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tà xwáyá í’í</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xwáyá</div>
<div class="gloss">run</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">í’í</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'I run'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (214)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tà xàní kàghá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàní</div>
<div class="gloss">sleep</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kàghá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">2SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'you sleep'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Topicalization of nominal subject in verbless clauses is marked through a variety of determiners before and after the subject:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (215)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>yà yá gwì’yán	yá dágálá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gwì’yán</div>
<div class="gloss">elephant</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dágálá</div>
<div class="gloss">large</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'that elephant is large'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (216)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>à á gwì’yán á dágálá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">à</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gwì’yán</div>
<div class="gloss">elephant</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dágálá</div>
<div class="gloss">large</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'that elephant over there is large'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Fronting is a coding means for topicalization of noun phrases. The fronted noun phrase is separated from the comment clause by the complementizer ná, identical with one of the demonstratives:</p>
<p>Topicalization of subject:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (217)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsá Gulu yá ná yà-yà tá zwànì ndá ndghà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">Gulu</div>
<div class="gloss">Gulu</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yà-yà</div>
<div class="gloss">give.birth-give.birth</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zwànì</div>
<div class="gloss">child:<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndghà</div>
<div class="gloss">many</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'that Gulu begot many children'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Topicalization of object:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (218)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xìyá xìyá skwì	txàf-í tà ná ɗèlèwèr ná ná skwì	3 nghá-nà-ghá-tsí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xìyá</div>
<div class="gloss">corn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xìyá</div>
<div class="gloss">corn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">skwì</div>
<div class="gloss">thing</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">txàf-í</div>
<div class="gloss">expel-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗèlèwèr</div>
<div class="gloss">notebook</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">skwì</div>
<div class="gloss">thing</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">3</div>
<div class="gloss">three</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">nghá-nà-ghá-tsí</div>
<div class="gloss">look-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-D:GO-3SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'what I have written about in this notebook regards three things' (cited from written sources where the numeral three was rendered by a digit 3)</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Topicalization of adjunct:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (219)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>índà	dimanche ná màmú marriage ndánà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">índà</div>
<div class="gloss">every</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dimanche</div>
<div class="gloss">sunday (fr.)</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">màmú</div>
<div class="gloss">exist</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">marriage</div>
<div class="gloss">marriage</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndánà</div>
<div class="gloss">now</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'every sunday there is a marriage now'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Focus">Focus</h2>
<p>Focus is marked by placing the element to be focused at the beginning of the clause and following it with the copula, most often <em>yà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (220)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà m̀ndú yà dágálá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">m̀ndú</div>
<div class="gloss">man</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dágálá</div>
<div class="gloss">important</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and the man is the most important person'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Focus may also be marked by the comment marker <em>tá</em> preceding the comment clause:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (221)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tíkvá gàvlì tá mn-áy kà-zlày ná sí m̀ndú dzì’í rà tá krì dzì’í</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tíkvá</div>
<div class="gloss">Tikva</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gàvlì</div>
<div class="gloss">Gavli</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mn-áy</div>
<div class="gloss">say-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà-zlày</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ-COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sí</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PAST</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">m̀ndú</div>
<div class="gloss">man</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzì’í</div>
<div class="gloss">kill-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">rà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">krì</div>
<div class="gloss">dog</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzì’í</div>
<div class="gloss">kill-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'it is Tikva Gali who said, "Is it a man that I killed? I killed a dog."'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The fronted noun phrase is interpreted as an object if the comment clause has an overtly marked subject. In the example below, the subject is marked by the unspecified human marker <em>lù</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (222)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsá yá skwì tà xgù-lù kà zə̀gláftà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">skwì</div>
<div class="gloss">thing</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xgù-lù</div>
<div class="gloss">call-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UH</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss">as</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zə̀gláftà</div>
<div class="gloss">zə̀gláftà</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'this is the thing that one calls zə̀gláftà'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Relative clause">Relative clause</h2>
<p>In the relative clause, the head precedes the comment clause. The head may be marked by a variety of determiners, depending on whether it is present in the environment of speech and whether it was mentioned in the previous discourse.</p>
<p>Relativization of the subject of verbal clauses obeys the same rules that apply in focus constructions. In the perfective aspect the relativized subject is followed by the comment-clause marker <em>tá</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (223)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>màmú	sàn m̀ghám tá kl-áf-tá màràkw	xìs</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">màmú</div>
<div class="gloss">exist</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sàn</div>
<div class="gloss">certain</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">m̀ghám</div>
<div class="gloss">chief</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kl-áf-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">take-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">màràkw</div>
<div class="gloss">wife</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xìs</div>
<div class="gloss">two</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'there was once a chief who married two wives'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The relativized noun phrase is interpreted as object when the relative clause has an overt subject. In the example below, the overt subject is the suffix <em>ì</em> (1SG) on the verb <em>txá-f-ì</em> ‘I wrote’:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (224)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xìyá-xìyá skwì	txá-f-ì tà ná ɗélèwèr ná ná...</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xìyá-xìyá</div>
<div class="gloss">corn-corn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">skwì</div>
<div class="gloss">thing</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">txá-f-ì</div>
<div class="gloss">expel-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗélèwèr</div>
<div class="gloss">book</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'the general themes that I have written about in this book . . . '</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Focus and relative clause constructions share a number of similarities, but there are also some differences. Both focus and relativization interact with the system of reference, with the aspectual system (only the dependent aspects can be used in comment-on-focus and relative clauses), and with polarity. For the full treatment of this topic, the reader is referred to chapter 19 of Frajzyngier with Shay 2002.</p>
<h2 id="Simultanious and sequential propositions">Simultanious and sequential propositions</h2>
<p>Hdi does not have a coordinated clausal conjunction ( cf. the section on locative extensions).
