Simultaneous propositions do not have a conjunction, and simultaneity is marked by clauses following each other. The presence of sequential clauses within the same sentence is indicated by the fact that the subject (if any) occurs only once, in the first clause:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (225)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>bàɗú xú’ú-á tsá zíndíŋ yá ngá 	dà tá mbízà ngá	làɓà-ná-f-tà ndá ghúv-à gù ngá 	vlá-n tá zwàn-ì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">bàɗú</div>
<div class="gloss">day</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xú’ú-á</div>
<div class="gloss">pound-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zíndíŋ</div>
<div class="gloss">germinated corn</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ngá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NORM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dà</div>
<div class="gloss">cook</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbízà</div>
<div class="gloss">bean dish</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ngá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NORM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">làɓà-ná-f-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">mix-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ghúv-à</div>
<div class="gloss">excrement-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">GEN</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gù</div>
<div class="gloss">goat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ngá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NORM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">vlá-n</div>
<div class="gloss">give-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zwàn-ì</div>
<div class="gloss">child-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PL</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'on the day of pounding the corn, one would cook a bean dish, 	mix it with goat excrement, and give it to children'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The sequential interpretation of events can be overtly marked by the conjunction <em>mbàɗ ká</em> ‘then’ followed by the sequential marker <em>kà</em>, or it may be marked only by the sequential marker <em>kà</em>: </p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (226)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>tsghà-dá-f xáxə̀n tá sànì lá-ghà-ní mbàɗ ká kà tsghà-dá-f-tá sànì zlíbí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsghà-dá-f</div>
<div class="gloss">put.up-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ALL-UP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xáxə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sànì</div>
<div class="gloss">one</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-ghà-ní</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:PVG-3SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbàɗ</div>
<div class="gloss">then</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsghà-dá-f-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">send-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ALL-UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sànì</div>
<div class="gloss">one</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">zlíbí</div>
<div class="gloss">bag</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'they sent up one bag, then they sent another bag'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The sequential marker <em>kà</em> is often followed by the verb <em>là</em> ‘go’, which has been grammaticalized as the marker of the sequential (Frajzyngier 2005):</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (227)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>lá-ghà pákáw ghúvì kày kà lá-b díngá-f-tá tsá mbízà yà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-ghà</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:PVG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">pákáẁ ghúvì</div>
<div class="gloss">hyena</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kày</div>
<div class="gloss">thus</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-b</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OUT</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">díngá-f-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">put.on.fire-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mbízà</div>
<div class="gloss">bean dish</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'after Hyena went, he put the bean dish on the fire'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Disjoint clauses">Disjoint clauses</h2>
<p>Clausal disjunction is coded by the form <em>á nà</em>. The form <em>nà</em> is probably identical with the interrogative marker <em>nà</em>: </p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (228)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>twák rí gù á nà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">twák</div>
<div class="gloss">sheep</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">rí</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">gù</div>
<div class="gloss">goat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">á nà</div>
<div class="gloss">or</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'is it a sheep or a goat?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (229)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>mágá-mágá rí mágà à wà á nà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mágá-mágá</div>
<div class="gloss">do-do</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">rí</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">Q</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mágá</div>
<div class="gloss">do</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">à</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">á nà</div>
<div class="gloss">or</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'did he do it or did he not?'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Counter-expectation clauses">Counter-expectation clauses</h2>
<p>Counter-expectation is marked by the conjunction <em>má</em>, <em>àmmá</em> or <em>àmá</em> ‘but’ (borrowed from either Hausa or Fula but originally coming from Arabic):</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (230)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ksá-f-tà dángwà t-íì kày mántsá wà lá-x-à-ɗá tà lòpitál má xàɗú kwóbù</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ksá-f-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">catch-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UP-REF:SUBJ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dángwà</div>
<div class="gloss">illness</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">t-íì</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ-1SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kày</div>
<div class="gloss">then</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mántsá</div>
<div class="gloss">then</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-x-à-ɗá</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DOWN-1SG-GO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lòpitál</div>
<div class="gloss">hospital (fr.)</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">má</div>
<div class="gloss">but</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàɗú</div>
<div class="gloss">lack</div>
</div>

<div class="morpheme">kwóbù</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'when I became ill, I went to a hospital, but there was no money then' ('When the illness caught me . . .')</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<h2 id="Complementation">Complementation</h2>
<h3 id="Formal means of marking">Formal means of marking</h3>
<p>The formal means used in complements of verbs of saying are used in complementation of other verbs. The verbs of saying include <em>ná</em> ‘say’, <em>lmá</em> ‘forbid’, <em>ɗáwá</em> ‘ask’, <em>txá</em> ‘expel’ [words], <em>gwàɗá</em> ‘talk’, and <em>zlày</em> ‘talk’. The complementizers occurring with these verbs are <em>ká</em>, <em>ká mántsá</em> both meaning ‘like that’, and <em>kà zlày</em>, consisting most probably of the sequential marker <em>kà</em> and the citation form of the verb <em>zlày</em> ‘talk’.</p>
<p>The complement clause of a verb of saying can precede or follow the matrix clause:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (231)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>lá ká-xə̀n mná-ná-tà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá</div>
<div class="gloss">go</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mná-ná-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">tell-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3SG-REF</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'they told him to go'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The complementizer precedes the matrix clause or may precede and follow the matrix clause:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (232)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ká yàgh mántsá ɗífà-úgh-ɗífà xád yà ká yàghí</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yàgh</div>
<div class="gloss">squirrel</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mántsá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗífà-úgh-ɗífà</div>
<div class="gloss">hide-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SO</span>-hide</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xád</div>
<div class="gloss">here</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">yàgh</div>
<div class="gloss">squirrel</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'squirrel said:"Hide yourself here"'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The important characteristics of the complement of verbs of saying is that the verb of the matrix clause does not have to be present:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (233)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>sá-ghá-sá ká-xə̀n ndá í’í</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sá-ghá-sá</div>
<div class="gloss">arrive-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:PVG</span>-arrive</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ká-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP-3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ASSC</span></div>
</div>

</div>
</div>

</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (234)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">

<h3 id="Complements of cognitive verbs">Complements of cognitive verbs</h3>
<p>The complement of the verb <em>sná</em> ‘know’, ‘hear’ may be marked by the complementizer <em>ká-’á</em> or <em>zlày</em> following the complement clause and the background marker <em>ná</em> following the matrix clause. In the following example the complement clause is marked by the complementizer <em>zlày</em> preceding the complement clause and the complementizer <em>ká-’á</em> following the complement clause:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (236)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">

<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">

<h2 id="Adjunct clauses">Adjunct clauses</h2>
<p>Temporal protasis clauses are marked by tone lowering on the verb-final morpheme before the subject:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (240)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>ndzdà-vá-tà ùvá tà xvá tà ǹghə́-l ná kà sá-ghá krì</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndzdà-vá-tà</div>
<div class="gloss">last-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AS-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ùvá</div>
<div class="gloss">cat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xvá</div>
<div class="gloss">work</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ǹghə́-l</div>
<div class="gloss">see-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">UH</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ná</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">sá-ghá</div>
<div class="gloss">arrive-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">D:PVG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">krì</div>
<div class="gloss">dog</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'when Cat had spent some time working on the field, one sees Dog coming'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Cf.:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (241)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà ndzɗà-vá-tá	ùvá tà xvá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ndzɗà-vá-tá</div>
<div class="gloss">stay-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">AS-REF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ùvá</div>
<div class="gloss">cat</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xvá</div>
<div class="gloss">work</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'and the cat spent some time working'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Another means of coding the temporal protasis is through the nominalization of a clause. In such clauses, the subject is coded by possessive rather than verbal subject pronouns. Nominal subjects are also coded as possessors. The protasis clause has the form Verb(-Extensions) Possessive subject. The verb occurs in the simple, i.e. non-reduplicated, form. No temporal particles of any kind have to be used. The temporal apodosis clause can be marked by the sequential marker <em>kà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (242)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>lá-mà	krì dá xàd-à kà hlà-ná-ghá-tá-tsí t-úvá</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lá-mà</div>
<div class="gloss">go-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IN</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">krì</div>
<div class="gloss">dog</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàd-à</div>
<div class="gloss">here-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">hlà-ná-ghá-tá-tsí</div>
<div class="gloss">find-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">DEM-D:PVG-REF-3SG</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">t-úvá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span>-cat</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'when Dog entered there, he found Cat'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>The temporal protasis clause may also be marked by a variety of markers coding anteriority, simultaneity, and posteriority of the protasis clause.</p>
<p>Purpose clauses are marked by the preposition <em>ngá</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (243)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>xàɗú kóɓù ngá mágà lèkól wà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">xàɗú</div>
<div class="gloss">lack</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kóɓù</div>
<div class="gloss">money</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ngá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FOR</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mágà</div>
<div class="gloss">do</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lèkól</div>
<div class="gloss">school</div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">wà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">NEG</span></div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'there was no money to go to school'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Reason clauses are marked by the subordinator <em>kàbgà</em>:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (244)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>dzà’á phlá-phlá-xə̀n tá m̀ndú,	kàbgà xáxə̀ŋ tá dzà-tá dá-ɗá ká gawa</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">dzà’á</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">FUT</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">phlá-phlá-xə̀n</div>
<div class="gloss">kill-kill-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">3PL</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">OBJ</span></div>
</div>

</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">

</div>

<div class="morpheme">tá</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COM</span></div>
</div>

</div>

<div class="gloss">father-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">1SG</span></div>
</div>

<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">COMP</span></div>

<div class="gloss">Gawa</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'"They will kill us all, because they killed my father", said Gawa'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In realis conditionals, the protasis clause is marked by the sequential marker <em>kà</em> in clause-initial position:</p>
<div class="sentence-wrapper">
<div class="sentence-number">
    (245)
</div>
<div class="sentence">
<div class="body">
<div class="object-language"><em>kà tà ɗv-áy lázgláftà</em></div>
<div class="gloss-box">
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">kà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">SEQ</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">tà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">IMPF</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">ɗv-áy</div>
<div class="gloss">like-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PO</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">lázgláftà</div>
<div class="gloss">god</div>
</div>
</div>
<div class="translation">'if god allows'</div>
</div>
</div>
</div>

<p>Irrealis conditionals are marked by the hypothetical marker má preceding the clause:</p>

</div>

</div>

</div>

<div class="gloss">stay-<span style="font-variant: small-caps;">ABS</span></div>
</div>
<div class="gloss-unit">
<div class="morpheme">mà</div>
<div class="gloss"><span style="font-variant: small-caps;">PREP</span></div>
</div>

<div class="gloss">Tourou</div>
</div>

<div class="translation">'if you wanted to live in Tourou . . .'</div>
</div>

<h2 id="Acknowledgments">Acknowledgments</h2>
<p>This dictionary is based on fieldwork that started in 1991. A number of Hdi speakers have shared their knowledge of the language: Romain Siloa Mbaka, the late Patrice Douka Prafé, Abel Ndjidda Kassie, Francis Barassoua Baigoua, Sikoa Sinowa, Benjamin Ngasnou, and Roger Prafé. Without their knowledge of Hdi this dictionary would not have been possible. </p>
<p>The dictionary incorporates data from Paul Eguchi’s (1971) “Matériaux pour servir à l’étude de la langue hidé: Vocabulaire.” Eguchi’s entries have been checked with respect to pronunciation and translation. In an email dated May 8, 2007, the late Paul Eguchi expressed his agreement to this incorporation and to being a co-author of the dictionary, as follows: “Yes, I’m interested in your project. If you can incorporate my material into the dictionary, it will be fine. It should be used in the right way, productive way. No dictionary can be perfect. Anyway, please go ahead with my material. I’m very happy to be a co-author of the new dictionary.” The co-authors express their sadness that, because of his premature passing, Paul Eguchi was not able to see the present work.</p>
<p>Roger Prafé has been the principal language assistant for the grammar of Hdi (Frajzyngier with Shay 2002) and for this dictionary. He took most of the photographs accompanying the dictionary, and he recorded all of the entries and examples. </p>
<p>Henry Tourneux has edited the French entries, translated many examples, and, most importantly, has pointed out erroneous translations of some flora and fauna terms. His help was extremely valuable. </p>
<p>Erin Shay has read through the introduction to the dictionary and made many valuable editorial suggestions. Megan Schwabauer has entered all the data into the Lexus database and introduced numerous corrections. She has also compiled the first versions of the English-Hdi-French and French-Hdi-English indexes. Several students at the University of Colorado participated in the work on this dictionary, including Thea Hongdoxmai. One summer Kristin Weis, who wasn’t a student, joined in the project just for intellectual satisfaction.</p>
<p>Will Styler helped with separating sound recordings into individual entries. </p>
<p>The work on this dictionary was supported by grants from the Humboldt Research Award, National Science Foundation, the University of Colorado, and more recently, by the CorTypo project funded by the Agence National de la Recherche.</p>
<p>We would like to thank Mrs Susanne Remmel M.A. for her careful proofreading of the manuscript and for numerous suggestions concerning the lay-out, glosses, and terms.</p>
<p>We are most grateful to Martin Haspelmath for the invitation to make the Dictionary available in the Dictionary journal, and to Iren Hartmann and her team for making it possible. It was not an easy task and it has been accomplished in a very short time. Without Iren’s effort, this dictionary would not have been made available with the sound recordings and the accompanying photographs. </p>
<p>While we are most grateful to all who helped with this work in so many ways, I alone am responsible for any errors and infelicities.</p>
